i\n3967:     e., ``V_sorted[(N-1)/2]``, when ``N`` is odd, and the average of the\n3968:     two middle values of ``V_sorted`` when ``N`` is even.\n3969: \n3970:     Examples\n3971:     --------\n3972:     >>> import numpy as np\n3973:     >>> a = np.array([[10, 7, 4], [3, 2, 1]])\n3974:     >>> a\n3975:     array([[10,  7,  4],\n3976:            [ 3,  2,  1]])\n3977:     >>> np.median(a)\n3978:     np.float64(3.5)\n3979:     >>> np.median(a, axis=0)\n3980:     array([6.5, 4.5, 2.5])\n3981:     >>> np.median(a, axis=1)\n3982:     array([7.,  2.])\n3983:     >>> np.median(a, axis=(0, 1))\n3984:     np.float64(3.5)\n3985:     >>> m = np.median(a, axis=0)\n3986:     >>> out = np.zeros_like(m)\n3987:     >>> np.median(a, axis=0, out=m)\n3988:     array([6.5,  4.5,  2.5])\n3989:     >>> m\n3990:     array([6.5,  4.5,  2.5])\n3991:     >>> b = a.copy()\n3992:     >>> np.median(b, axis=1, overwrite_input=True)\n3993:     array([7.,  2.])\n3994:     >>> assert not np.all(a==b)\n3995:     >>> b = a.copy()\n3996:     >>> np.median(b, axis=None, overwrite_input=True)\n3997:     np.float64(3.5)\n3998:     >>> assert not np.all(a==b)\n3999: \n4000:     \"\"\"\n4001:     return _ureduce(a, func=_median, keepdims=keepdims, axis=axis, out=out,\n4002:                     overwrite_input=overwrite_input)\n4003: \n4004: \n4005: def _median(a, axis=None, out=None, overwrite_input=False):\n4006:     # can't be reasonably be implemented in terms of percentile as we have to\n4007:     # call mean to not break astropy\n4008:     a = np.asanyarray(a)\n4009: \n4010:     # Set the partition indexes\n4011:     if axis is None:\n4012:         sz = a.size\n4013:     else:\n4014:         sz = a.shape[axis]\n4015:     if sz % 2 == 0:\n4016:         szh = sz // 2\n4017:         kth = [szh - 1, szh]\n4018:     else:\n4019:         kth = [(sz - 1) // 2]\n4020: \n4021:     # We have to check for NaNs (as of writing 'M' doesn't actually work).\n4022:     supports_nans = np.issubdtype(a.dtype, np.inexact) or a.dtype.kind in 'Mm'\n4023:     if supports_nans:\n4024:         kth.append(-1)\n4025: \n4026:     if overwrite_input:\n4027:         if axis is None:\n4028:             part = a.ravel()\n4029:             part.partition(kth)\n4030:         else:\n4031:             a.partition(kth, axis=axis)\n4032:             part = a\n4033:     else:\n4034:         part = partition(a, kth, axis=axis)\n4035: \n4036:     if part.shape == ():\n4037:         # make 0-D arrays work\n4038:         return part.item()\n4039:     if axis is None:\n4040:         axis = 0\n4041: \n4042:     indexer = [slice(None)] * part.ndim\n4043:     index = part.shape[axis] // 2\n4044:     if part.shape[axis] % 2 == 1:\n4045:         # index with slice to allow mean (below) to work\n4046:         indexer[axis] = slice(index, index+1)\n4047:     else:\n4048:         indexer[axis] = slice(index-1, index+1)\n4049:     indexer = tuple(indexer)\n4050: \n4051: ","url":"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/numpy--v2.2.2@9ca88bff35bf60de74f9f95e6f90e6b4e0913e78/-/blob/numpy/lib/_function_base_impl.py%3FL3910-4050"}}}

Default is -1 (last axis).\n        For now, only 1-D arrays and axis=-1 or axis=0 are fully supported.\n    mode : {'valid', 'same', 'full'}, optional\n        Method for handling the boundaries:\n\n        - 'valid': output size = input size - window size + 1.\n          The window is computed only at positions where it fully overlaps with\n          the input array.\n        - 'same': output size = input size. Pads the input as necessary.\n        - 'full': output size = input size + window size - 1.\n          The window is allowed to partially overlap with the input array.\n\n        Default is 'valid'.\n\n    Returns\n    -------\n    rolling_median : ndarray\n        An array containing the rolling median.\n        The shape of the output depends on the `mode` parameter.\n\n    See Also\n    --------\n    numpy.median, numpy.lib.stride_tricks.as_strided\n\n    Notes\n    -----\n    For each window position, the median is computed over all elements in the\n    window at that position.\n\n    The rolling median is useful for smoothing time series data and removing\n    outliers while preserving edges.\n\n    Examples\n    --------\n    >>> import numpy as np\n    >>> from numpy.lib import rolling_median\n    >>> a = np.array([1, 2, 3, 4, 5])\n    >>> rolling_median(a, 3)\n    array([2., 3., 4.])\n    >>> rolling_median(a, 3, mode='same')\n    array([1.5, 2. , 3. , 4. , 4.5])\n    >>> rolling_median(a, 3, mode='full')\n    array([1. , 1.5, 2. , 3. , 4. , 4.5, 5. ])\n    \"\"\"\n    a = np.asarray(a)\n\n    # Validate mode\n    if mode not in ('valid', 'same', 'full'):\n        raise ValueError(f\"mode must be one of 'valid', 'same', or 'full', got {mode}\")\n\n    # Normalize axis\n    if a.ndim == 0:\n        raise ValueError(\"rolling_median requires at least 1-D input\")\n\n    if axis < 0:\n        axis = a.ndim + axis\n    if axis < 0 or axis >= a.ndim:\n        raise np.AxisError(axis, a.ndim)\n\n    # Flatten to 2-D for easier processing: (..., last_dim)\n    a_flat = a.reshape(-1, last_dim)\n    n_rows = a_flat.shape[0]\n\n    if window_size > last_dim and mode == 'valid':\n        # Valid mode with window larger than array - return empty result\n        out_shape = list(original_shape)\n        out_shape[-1] = 0\n        result = np.empty(out_shape, dtype=a.dtype if np.issubdtype(a.dtype, np.integer) else np.float64)\n        if axis != a.ndim - 1:\n            result = np.moveaxis(result, -1, axis)\n        return result\n\n    # Compute rolling median for each row\n    if mode == 'valid':\n        out_size = last_dim - window_size + 1\n    elif mode == 'same':\n        out_size = last_dim\n    else:  # 'full'\n        out_size = last_dim + window_size - 1\n\n    # Determine output dtype\n    if np.issubdtype(a.dtype, np.integer):\n        out_dtype = np.float64\n    else:\n        out_dtype = a.dtype\n\n    result_flat = np.zeros((n_rows, out_size), dtype=out_dtype)\n\n    for i in range(out_size):\n        if mode == 'valid':\n            start = i\n            end = i + window_size\n        elif mode == 'same':\n            start = i - window_size // 2\n            end = start + window_size\n        else:  # 'full'\n            start = i - window_size + 1\n            end = i + 1\n\n        # Handle boundaries for 'same' and 'full' modes\n        actual_start = max(0, start)\n        actual_end = min(last_dim, end)\n\n        if actual_start < actual_end:\n            for row_idx in range(n_rows):\n                window = a_flat[row_idx, actual_start:actual_end]\n                result_flat[row_idx, i] = np.median(window)\n        else:\n            # Window is completely outside the array bounds\n            result_flat[:, i] = np.nan\n\n    # Reshape result back to original shape\n    out_shape = list(original_shape)\n    out_shape[-1] = out_size\n    result = result_flat.reshape(out_shape)\n\n    # Must be a positive integer.\n    axis : int, optional\n        Axis along which the rolling median is computed. Pads the input as necessary.\n        - 'full': output size = input size + window size - 1.\n          The window is allowed to partially overlap with the input array.\n\n        Default is 'valid'.\n\n    Returns\n    -------\n    rolling_median : ndarray\n        An array containing the rolling median.\n        The shape of the output depends on the `mode` parameter.\n\n    See Also\n    --------\n    numpy.median, numpy.lib.stride_tricks.as_strided\n\n    Notes\n    -----\n    For each window position, the median is computed over all elements in the\n    window at that position.\n\n    The rolling median is useful for smoothing time series data and removing\n    outliers while preserving edges.\n\n    Examples\n    --------\n    >>> import numpy as np\n    >>> from numpy.lib._rolling_median import rolling_median\n    >>> a = np.array([1, 2, 3, 4, 5])\n    >>> rolling_median(a, 3)\n    array([2., 3., 4.])\n    >>> rolling_median(a, 3, mode='same')\n    array([1.5, 2. , 3. , 4. , 4.5])\n    >>> rolling_median(a, 3, mode='full')\n    array([1. , 1.5, 2. , 3. , 4. , 4.5, 5. ])\n    \"\"\"\n    a = np.asarray(a)\n\n    #
